## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (single-species population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics in ecology. Typical relationships express dP_dt as per-capita growth times P, with density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects, external forcing in time t (seasonality), and/or removals (harvesting).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Linear time-trend in growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually changing environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Logistic growth ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density dependence; with c1 < 0 gives carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible density dependence curvature; c1 < 0)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (density dependence acting on log-population; choose c1 to represent 1/K scaling)
- Richards (generalized logistic) form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2)**c3 (extra shape parameters for asymmetric approach to saturation)
- Allee effect (strong) logistic-type: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (Allee threshold via P + c1 with c1 < 0; plus crowding via c2 < 0)
- Allee effect (weak) per-capita depression: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * P)) (reduced growth at low P transitioning with P)
- Constant harvesting (quota): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (c1 < 0 represents constant removal; extinction possible at low P)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P (net per-capita rate c0 + c1, with c1 < 0 for removal)
- Saturating harvesting (Holling type II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P / (P + c2) (removal saturates at high P due to handling/effort limits)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affects births/deaths)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity (via density term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P) (time-varying crowding strength/capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth modeling: expressing dP_dt as P * g(P,t) encodes that births/deaths scale with current population size.
- Crowding / carrying-capacity effects: negative nonlinear dependence on P (e.g., adding a term like c * P**2 inside dP_dt) produces slowing growth and possible equilibrium.
- Flexible density dependence: replacing P with P**c (theta-logistic) changes whether regulation is weak at low P and strong near capacity (c>1) or vice versa (0<c<1).
- Gompertz-type regulation: log-dependence (P * log(·)) implies per-capita growth declines approximately linearly with log(P), often fitting microbial/tumor-like growth.
- Allee effects: factors that change sign near a small-P threshold (e.g., P + c with c<0) create negative growth at low density and bistability (extinction vs persistence).
- Harvest/removal signatures: additive negative constants (quota) can drive extinction regardless of P, while proportional terms (∝ P) shift the effective per-capita rate.
- Saturating removal: rational terms like P/(P+c) represent limited harvesting/predation capacity, strong impact at low–moderate P and bounded impact at high P.
- Seasonality/forcing in time: sinusoidal dependence on t produces periodic modulation of growth rate and can induce oscillatory transients in P even without predator-prey coupling.
- Time-varying regulation: letting density-dependence coefficients depend on t models changing resources/capacity; this can shift equilibria over time and create tracking dynamics.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG14)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P + c6*P*exp(-c7*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

Let  
\[
GT(t,P)=a\Big[(1-\tfrac{P}{b})P+(1-e^{-kP})P+P e^{-kt}\Big]
\]
with fixed \(a=0.11423898258902421\), \(b=40.69810220267985\), \(k=0.08368363514073095\).

So GT has these structural properties:

- As a function of \(P\): it contains a **quadratic polynomial part** \(a(P-\frac{P^2}{b})\) **plus** a **non-polynomial exponential-in-\(P\)** term \(-a\,P e^{-kP}\) (because \(a(1-e^{-kP})P=aP-aPe^{-kP}\)).
- As a function of \(t\): it contains a term \(aP e^{-kt}\), i.e. **\(t\) appears only inside an exponential decay and is multiplied by \(P\)**.
- There are **no** \(\sin\), \(\cos\), \(\log\), rational \(1/(P+\cdot)\), \(1/P\), etc.

A candidate can match only if it can simultaneously reproduce:
1) a \(P e^{-kP}\) term (exponential in \(P\) multiplied by \(P\), with negative coefficient), and  
2) a \(P e^{-kt}\) term (exponential in \(t\) multiplied by \(P\)), and  
3) the polynomial \(aP - aP^2/b\), and  
4) no extra functional forms.

Now check each candidate.

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P + c2 t + c3 + c4 e^{c5\sin(c6 t+c7)}\)
Has \(t\) linearly and inside \(\sin\) inside \(\exp\); no \(P e^{-kP}\) and no \(P e^{-kt}\) (the exponential term is independent of \(P\)). Cannot match.

### 2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 t + c3\log(Pc4+1)+c5+c6 e^{Pc7}+c8 t\)
Has \(P e^{Pc7}\) possible (via \(c6 e^{Pc7}\)) but GT needs \(P e^{-kP}\), i.e. exponential multiplied by \(P\). Here exponential term is not multiplied by \(P\). Also has \(\log\) and \(Pt\) terms not in GT. Cannot match.

### 3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P + c2 + c3\log(c4 t+1) + c5 t (P+c6)^{c7}\)
Has \(\log\) in \(t\) and power term \(t(P+\cdot)^{c7}\); GT has only \(P e^{-kt}\) in \(t\). Cannot match.

### 4. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + c4 t + c5 + c6 e^{c7\sin(c8 t+c9)}\)
Only polynomial in \(P\); \(t\) linear and sinusoidal-exponential. No \(P e^{-kP}\) or \(P e^{-kt}\). Cannot.

### 5. Same issue as 4 (extra \(+P\) doesn’t help). Cannot.

### 6. Polynomial in \(P\) plus \(t\) linear plus sinusoidal-exponential independent of \(P\). No required exponentials. Cannot.

### 7. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(c4 t+c5)+c6+c7\log(c8 t+1)\)
Has \(\sin\) and \(\log\) in \(t\); no exponentials. Cannot.

### 8. Polynomial in \(P\) plus \(t\) linear plus sinusoidal-exponential. No. Cannot.

### 9. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(\cdot) + P^{c6}c7 + c8\)
No exponentials in \(P\) or \(t\). Cannot.

### 10. Polynomial + \(\log(Pc4+1)\) + rational terms \(1/(Pc7+c8)\) and \(c9/P\). GT has none of these. Cannot.

### 11. Polynomial + \(\log(c4 t+1)\) + \(e^{Pc6}\cos(\cdot)\). Wrong functional forms; also exponential in \(P\) not multiplied by \(P\) and includes cosine. Cannot.

### 12. Has \(P^{c2} t\), \(e^{c5 t}\), \(\log(t)\). GT needs \(P e^{-kt}\) and \(P e^{-kP}\). Cannot.

### 13. Polynomial + \(\log(Pc4+1)\) + \(c5/(P+c6)\) + \(c8/P\) + linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 14. Same as 13 plus \(Pc2\). Still has logs/rationals. Cannot.

### 15. Polynomial + \(c4/(P+c5)\) + linear \(t\). No exponentials; has rational. Cannot.

### 16. Contains \(P\log(Pc4+1)\) and \(P\log(Pc7+1)\). GT has exponentials, not logs. Cannot.

### 17. Adds \(\log(c8 e^{c9 t}+1)\) and rational \(1/(P+c5)\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 18. Logs and rationals. Cannot.

### 19. Has \(P\log(Pc4+1)\) and linear \(t\). No. Cannot.

### 20. Purely polynomial in \(P\) plus \(P\log(Pc5+1)\) and linear \(t\). No. Cannot.

### 21. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + Pc4 + Pc5 + c6 + c7/(P+c8) + c9 t\)
This has a \(P e^{Pc3}\) term (good shape for \(P e^{-kP}\) if \(c3=-k\)). But:
- It also has a rational \(c7/(P+c8)\) which must be removed by setting \(c7=0\) (ok).
- It has linear \(t\) term \(c9 t\) which must be 0 (set \(c9=0\)).
- **Crucially, it has no \(P e^{-kt}\) term** (no exponential in \(t\) multiplied by \(P\)). So cannot match.

### 22. Has \(P\log(\cdot)\) terms and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 23. Has \(e^{Pc4}\) (not multiplied by \(P\)), and rational-in-\(P\) terms with \(t/(Pc6+c7)\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 24. Has \(P\log(\cdot)\), rational \(1/(P+c7)\), and extra \(1/(P+c7)\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 25. Polynomial + linear \(t\) + sinusoidal-exponential. No. Cannot.

### 26. Polynomial + linear \(t\) + sinusoidal-exponential. No. Cannot.

### 27. Has \(P\log(\cdot)\) and rational \(c6/(P+c7)\) and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 28. Has \(P c2 e^{Pc3}\) (could mimic \(P e^{-kP}\)) but \(t\) appears as \(t^{c6}\) and \(\log(c9 t+1)\), not as \(P e^{-kt}\). Cannot.

### 29. Has \(e^{Pc4}\) not multiplied by \(P\), plus rationals. Cannot.

### 30. Has \(e^{Pc4}\) not multiplied by \(P\), plus rational terms. Cannot.

### 31. Logs and rationals. Cannot.

### 32. Polynomial + \(\sin(c5 t+c6)\) + linear \(t\). No exponentials. Cannot.

### 33. Has \(e^{Pc4}\) not multiplied by \(P\), rationals \(1/(P+c7)\), \(c8/P\), and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 34. Has \(P c2 e^{Pc3}\) but \(t\) only inside \(\log(c7 t+1)\) (not \(P e^{-kt}\)). Cannot.

### 35. Has \(e^{Pc5}\) (not multiplied by \(P\)) and \(P c2 t\) and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 36. Has rational \(c3/(P+c4)\), \(\log(c7 e^{c8 t}+1)\), linear \(t\). No \(P e^{-kt}\) term; also wrong forms. Cannot.

### 37. Has \(P c1 e^{Pc2}\) and \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\) (could create \(P e^{-kP}\) plus another), but \(t\) only in \(\log(c9 t+1)\), not \(P e^{-kt}\). Cannot.

### 38. Has \(e^{c4 t}\) but **not multiplied by \(P\)**; also has rational \(c6/(P+c7)\) and linear \(t\). Cannot.

### 39. Has \(P\log(\cdot)\) and \(\log(Pc7+1)\) and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 40. Has \(P^{c2} e^{c4 t}\) and \(e^{c6 t}\) and \(\log(t)\). Even if \(c2=1\) gives \(P e^{c4 t}\), it still lacks the \(P e^{-kP}\) term and includes extra \(e^{c6 t}\) and \(\log\). Cannot.

### 41. Has \(\log(c4 t+1)\) and \(e^{c6\sin(\cdot)}\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 42. Has \(P c2 e^{Pc3}\) and \(P^{c5}c6\) and linear \(t\). No \(P e^{-kt}\). Cannot.

### 43. Has \(e^{Pc4}\) (not multiplied by \(P\)) and \(\log(t)\). Cannot.

### 44. Has \(e^{Pc7}\) (not multiplied by \(P\)) and linear \(t\). Cannot.

### 45. Has rational and product of logs \(\log(Pc8+1)\log(c9 t+1)\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 46. Has rational-in-\(P\) terms and \(P c6 t\) and linear \(t\). Not GT. Cannot.

### 47. Same issues as 45 plus extra rational. Cannot.

### 48. Logs and rationals. Cannot.

### 49. Has \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\) (good for \(P e^{-kP}\)) but \(t\) only in \(\log(c8 t+1)\), not \(P e^{-kt}\). Cannot.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG14)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P + c6*P*exp(-c7*t)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
0.11424*(1 - P/40.698)*P + 0.11424*(1 - exp(-0.08368*P))*P + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

Expanding:
```
0.11424*P - 0.11424*P²/40.698 + 0.11424*P - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P) + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

Simplifying:
```
-0.002807*P² + 0.22848*P - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P) + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

The GT has these basis function components:
1. **P²** term (quadratic in P)
2. **P** term (linear in P)
3. **P·exp(-c·P)** term (P times exponential in P)
4. **P·exp(-c·t)** term (P times exponential in t)

This is crucial: the GT contains both `P*exp(α*P)` and `P*exp(β*t)` as essential basis functions.

Now let me check each candidate for the presence of these required basis functions.

### Key basis functions needed:
- P² ✓ (polynomial)
- P ✓ (polynomial)
- P·exp(c·P) — exponential in P multiplied by P
- P·exp(c·t) — exponential in t multiplied by P

Let me systematically check candidates:

**Candidate 1:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + P + c2*t + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(c6*t+c7))`
Has P², P terms. No P*exp(cP) term. No P*exp(ct) term. The exp(sin) term doesn't depend on P. Cannot match.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*t + c3*log(Pc4+1) + c5 + c6*exp(Pc7) + c8*t`
Has P², P, exp(P*c7), log(P*c4+1). Has P*c2*t (cross term). No P*exp(ct). The exp(Pc7) is not multiplied by P. log is not exp. Cannot match.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + P + c2 + c3*log(c4*t+1) + c5*t*(P+c6)^c7`
No P*exp(cP). The power term t*(P+c6)^c7 is not the right form. Cannot match.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `P²c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + c4*t + c5 + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t+c9))`
No P*exp(cP). No P*exp(ct). Cannot match.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]
